==PAGE:72==
7. Grid Connection
During a wind farm project the grid connection must be considered since it is an integral
part of the planning process and is treated in this chapter. First the possible points of
connection are studied followed by the chosen voltage level. Then the array cable length
is estimated for the project. The proposed project consist of 5 wind turbines with a total
capacity of 20 MW.
7.1
Point of connection
In order to decide the most appropriate point of connection (POC) the location of the
nearby connection points is studied for the sites of Sidinge Fjord and Fårevejle. The
available transformer stations for the national grid has been found through the Danish
Energy Agency as seen in appendix B ﬁgure B.1 where nearby connection points are lo-
cated in Nr. Asmindrup and Torslunde. However, the voltage level for these connection
points are 132/50 kV and is not suited for a wind park with a small capacity since the
cost would increase signiﬁcantly. Therefore the possibility to connect to the local grid
would be more reasonable due to the lower transmission level, this would also decrease
the cost of connection.
Contact has been made in order to locate the nearby transformer stations with Cerius
[5] , the local grid company in the municipality. The provided maps which can be seen
in appendix B ﬁgure B.2 and B.3 have been imported into Google Earth in order to
measure the distance from turbines to POC. In ﬁgure 7.1 the nearby transformer stations
are observed for the site in Sidinge Fjord.
Both stations are 50/10 kV stations and
therefore the selection of POC would be based on distance from turbines to POC as well
as the present load of the transformer station. North to Vig the ﬁrst station is observed
with a distance of 5.27 km. Although the future biogas plant is located near Vig with a
expected electricity production of 24.3 GWh [52] it is most likely planned to connect at
this station and could bring challenges on coping with the grid. Besides the connection
of the bio-gas plant there are several turbines close to the transformer station. Figure
1.1 illustrates the existing turbines in the municipality where it is observed how most
of the turbines in the municipality are located close to the station and are most likely
connected to this point. However, it should be mentioned that the turbines have a very
low capacity compared to the new modern turbines with a total capacity of approximately
58
==PAGE:73==
3 MW and these turbines are almost ready for decommissioning as illustrated in table
3.1. Furthermore, it is noticed that the remaining turbines do not have a capacity above
100 kW which can be seen in appendix C table C.1. The second station located near
Grevinge has a greater distance of 6.71 km though with less nearby turbines that could
be connected to the station. It should be mentioned that the grid company is obligated
to couple the turbines to the nearest 50-60 kV station and strengthen the grid if needed
[3]. The grid strength indicates a strong POC as the short circuit power is expressed
in VA and is scaled with the square of the voltage, S = V 2
Z . Due to the obligation to
strengthen the grid if necessary by the grid company and a closer distance to POC the
decision is made to connect the three Siemens SWT-4.0-120 turbines to the station north
to Vig.
Figure 7.1: Connection point at 50/10 kV station in Sidinge Fjord
As for the site in Fårevejle two transformer stations are observed in ﬁgure 7.2. Both
with the voltage level of 50/10 kV. The station located in Grevinge is the same station
that was analyzed for the coupling at Sidinge Fjord. The distance from the turbines in
Fårevejle to the station is 6.73 km, while the other station located at Ris is only 3.21 km
away. Thus the decision is made to connect the two turbines in Fårevejle to the station
in Ris.
59
==PAGE:74==
Figure 7.2: Connection point at 50/10 kV station in Fårevejle.
7.1.1
Internal and export voltage
The selected turbine have the asynchronous generator with a nominal voltage of 690 V
see data sheet in appendix E. To avoid large ohmic losses in the array network this must
be stepped up. Due to the POC being a 50/10 kV station the export voltage should be
chosen to 10 or 50 kV. The connection models of the transformer for the export level
of 10 and 50 kV can be seen in appendix B ﬁgure B.4. Exporting at a voltage level of
10 kV could lead to a high transmission loss though the cost would be low, while the
export level of 50 kV leads to a low transmission loss and high costs. The decision will
then be made based on the voltage level that results in the lowest cost of connection [3].
The expenses of establishment, operation, maintenance and transmission loss up until
the POC will be held by the project owner [3]. Therefore the lowest cost of connection
is desired. Making an estimate of the grid strength for the two sites an approximate of
the short circuit power are taken from the lecture notes [8] for a grid voltage of 10 kV.
In order to have a strong grid strength the ratio between wind farm capacity and short
circuit power should be in the range 2-20 %. The estimation yielded 8 % for Sidinge with
three turbines and 5 % for Fårevejle with two turbines making the export voltage of 10
kV a reasonable choice. The internal array voltage is then chosen to 10 kV which the
in-turbine transformers must deliver for the project. While the export level voltage is
also chosen to 10 kV. The power is then transmitted as AC with the HVAC conﬁguration
due to the short distance to the grid and low capacity [8].
60
==PAGE:75==
7.1.2
Cable length estimate
Although the project is of small size, the estimation of cable length is an important
matter to discuss, as it plays a role in the economic point of view and could have an
environmental impact. Since, no collision risk was identiﬁed during the EIA, where only
the area of Nykøbing Sjælland was an important area for the birds and with the overhead
lines being a more eﬃcient and cheap solution compared to the underground cable the
decision is made to connect with overhead lines to the POC. The cable length is estimated
for the two sites in Fårevejle and Sidinge Fjord. Figure 7.1 and 7.2 illustrates the location
of the turbines along with the distances to the POC that is used for the estimation of
the total cable length. For Sidinge Fjord the distance to the connection point is approx.
6.6 km while the remaining two turbines in Fårevejle have a distance of 3.8 km to POC
yielding a total cable length of 10.4 km. The decision to connect to the local grid rather
than the national grid brings a number of advantages, this decreases the cost of connection
greatly since an additional transformer is not needed as well as the cable length which
has been decreased from 17 km to 10.4 km. With the decrease of cable length it is also
expected a decrease in the environmental impact.
61
==PAGE:76==
8. Project Economy
From chapter 6 it was found that the proposed project would consist of ﬁve wind turbines
with a total installed capacity of 20 MW. In this chapter the economic feasibility of the
proposed project is studied. First the assumptions behind the calculation is presented.
Then the key ﬁnancial of the project is reported. Lastly a sensitivity analysis of the
results is carried out which concludes the chapter.
8.1
Financial assumptions
In order to carry out the calculations of the economic analysis ﬁnancial assumptions is
needed. In table 8.1 the assumptions is summarized followed with an elaboration of the
chosen values below.
Figure
Unit
Value
Reference
Capital Investment
DKK/MW
6.000.000
[15]

DKK/MWh
60
[57]
Electricity Price
DKK/MWh
291
[42]

%
6
[20]

years
20
[29]
Table 8.1: Financial assumptions of the proposed project
The cost of a wind turbine is by rule of thumb set to be 7 mil. DKK/ MW however
a decrease by 25% by Siemens Gamesa and Vestas in 2018 shows that the cost of wind
turbines was decreased to approx. 5.5 mil. DKK/MW for onshore turbines [15]. Thus
the chosen estimate is based on the updated prices with the addition of the cost of grid
connection which is typically around 9% [32]. Next the O&M cost is set to 60 DKK/MWh
since the Danish Wind Turbine Association has estimated this for wind turbines with a
capacity above 2 MW.
The day-ahead market is the primary market for trading with electricity where suppliers
and producers try to cover the electricity demand for the following day. The suppliers
will then bid in the market where the market price will be set by the activated production
with the highest bid. Often the producers bid their market price at their marginal cost
which is done in order to get activated in the market. The marginal cost for solar and
wind power is the lowest while the high marginal costs is observed at the coal plants.
62
==PAGE:77==
Having said that, there is a great uncertainty on the future electricity prices and it is
very diﬃcult to predict in the future. Nevertheless, there are some factors that aﬀect the
future prices. The most important factor of the future prices is the fuel and CO2 prices,
especially the coal prices which play an important role since the electricity price is pri-
marily set by the coal price[10]. With a decrease in the fuel and CO2 prices in the recent
years, the marginal cost of coal and gas-ﬁred plants has been lowered compared to the
previous years resulting in decreased electricity price. This is backed up by studies con-
ducted from the Danish Energy Agency which show that there is a close relation between
the coal marginal and electricity prices. When there is a decline in the coal marginal
the electricity price also decreases[10]. Other factors as dry years and wet years as well
as transmission capacity to neighbouring areas also play a role in the future electricity
prices. In a dry year the electricity prices increase signiﬁcantly while it decreases in a wet
year in the North. The hydro plants with reservoirs will often bid in with a price similar
to the coal marginal in order to increase their revenue. The expansion of the transmission
capacity from Denmark and the Nordic countries to the rest of Northern Europe has also
a signiﬁcance for the prices due to the Nordic overproduction in a normal and wet year[10].
Due to the great uncertainty on electricity prices, the chosen electricity price has been
estimated by analyzing the market price for the Nord Pool where the yearly prices in
the time period of 2003-2018 has been averaged for DK2 (Zealand), this is deemed as a
reasonable estimate since the electricity price is constantly varying. Furthermore, it is
observed from the Nord Pool that the electricity price for DK2 has increased after the
abolition of subsidies in February 2018 [14]. This makes sense since the producer has
to bid in the day ahead market at higher prices as no subsidies are provided[42]. The
lifetime of a turbine is usually between 20-25 years where 20 years is chosen to ensure a
reasonable economic analysis. Furthermore the capacity factor is estimated to 0.32 based
on the total production and capacity of the turbines. Lastly the discount rate has been
selected based on the renewable energy discount rate survey [20].
8.2
Key Financial Figures
The key ﬁnancial ﬁgures are illustrated in table 8.2. It is seen that the IRR is greater
than the discount rate, stating that the project would be feasible. Furthermore it is seen
that the yearly net income is approx. 13 mil. DKK. While the yearly O&M cost 3.36
mil. DKK.

8.3
Sensitivity analysis
In this section a sensitivity analysis is treated with respect to the IRR and NPV, capital
investment and the discount rate. This is done for varying electricity prices.
With the computed P50 AEP estimate for the 5 Siemens turbines seen in table 6.1 the
relation between IRR and NPV as a function of the electricity price is investigated. In
ﬁgure 8.1 the results is illustrated where the calculations is carried out using the stated
assumptions.
Figure 8.1: NPV, IRR vs electricity price
With constantly varying electricity prices on the market, it is important to analyze if
the project would be proﬁtable when taking varying prices in consideration. The ﬁgure
illustrates that the project is feasible with the assumed electricity price. However, when
the price decreases to 231 DKK/MWh IRR becomes 6.3 % which is a critical value since
the assumed discount rate is 6 %. Therefore the electricity price should not fall below
this value as the IRR will be less than the discount rate resulting in a non-proﬁtable
project. The underlying calculations can be seen in appendix J.
64
==PAGE:79==
Figure 8.2: Sensitivity analysis NPV as a function of the capital investment
In ﬁgure 8.2 it is noticed how the NPV decreases linearly with increasing capital invest-
ment for the three electricity prices. The small diﬀerence in NPV is an indication of the
small variation of 20 DKK/MWh for the three diﬀerent prices. In order to have a feasible
project the NPV has to be greater then zero [50]. It is observed that the project economy
is sensitive to the capital investment where the NPV starts becomes negative at approx.
7 mil. DKK/MW for a electricity price of 271 DKK/MWh. While a capital investment
above 7.2 mil. DKK/MW lead to a non-proﬁtable project with the electricity price of
291 DKK/MWh. It is expected that with decreasing electricity prices the NPV would be
negative at lower capital investments. It should be mentioned, however, that the wind
turbine manufacturers are constantly working towards lowering the cost of turbines as
mentioned in [15].
65
==PAGE:80==
Figure 8.3: Sensitivity analysis NPV as a function of the discount rate
The sensitivity of the discount rate is illustrated in ﬁgure 8.3. It is observed that the
discount rate has a high sensitivity since the NPV becomes negative at a discount rate
of 8 % for the 271 DKK/MWh electricity price.
Furthermore it can be seen that a
higher electricity price is needed as the discount rate increases in order to keep having a
proﬁtable project. Lastly, it can be concluded that the proposed project will be proﬁtable
with a yearly net income of approx. 13 mil. DKK.

Table 9.1: Overview of stakeholders
The tourism associations are believed to have the highest signiﬁcance of the project
acceptance. There are several associations regarding tourism in the municipality. The
most inﬂuential ones are the Odsherred Geopark and the Tourist Board Visit Odsherred
which represent the major part of the activities for tourists also explained in section
1.3.2. In the EIA report, described in chapter 4, the cottage areas were considered to be
critical areas for wind turbine sites. The two turbine sites, Sidinge Fjord and Fårevejle,
were selected due to the small amount of cottage areas observed, therefore, the cottage
owners are not explained in this chapter. A detailed explanation of the stakeholders can
be found in appendix I. Lastly, to have an better insight of the locals attitude toward
wind turbines, the paradigm shift in ownership models will be explained and presented.
9.1.1
Approach
The phase of project acceptance can be diﬃcult if the turbine sites are placed inside the
areas which the Geopark describe as the characteristic landscape of Odsherred[19]. The
67
==PAGE:82==
project has from the start been based on not locating turbine sites inside these valuable
areas. This chapter will elaborate the information obtained during the communication
process with the stakeholders; their ideas and opinions toward the project will be used
to conﬁrm the quality of the results achieved up until now. Also, a beneﬁcial solution
between the municipality and the key holders of the tourism sector will be developed in
order to ease the process of project acceptance.
9.2
Odsherred Municipality
The communication with Odsherred municipality was kept during the whole project de-
velopment. Since the start of the project, the municipality has expressed their fears about
the bad inﬂuence a wind project possibly could have on the tourism. The communication
has been accomplished by monthly meetings in the town hall of Odsherred. The con-
tact person has been the climate coordinator Simone Veber. Her ideas have been used as
guidance to the project where some of the turbine sites described in chapter 4 were shown
to Simone to learn her opinions on the sites. Apart from the sites, the tourism of the
municipality has been the main topic during the meetings. The municipality wants their
inhabitants to understand how important a wind project is to the global climate changes.
Brainstorming and idea exchange have been the approach to ﬁnd a solution regarding
this. Since the municipality guests many tourists during the summer and Sommerland
Sjælland being a huge attraction for the visitors, a symbolic turbine placed close to the
area was decided to be an good investment. The idea was inspired by the Ikea turbine
placed next to Ikea Taastrup [47]. The turbine will be visible from the park entrance to
its visitors. However, this idea will be elaborated in section 9.4. Lastly, Simone agreed
to the fact that the Geopark and Visit Odsherred being the most signiﬁcant stakeholders
regarding tourism. Since Visit Odsherred as well as Sommerland Sjælland are parts of
the Odsherred Geopark, contact to the director Hans-Jørgen Olsen was made.
9.3
Geopark Odsherred and Visit Odsherred
The Geopark and Visit Odsherred is without a doubt the most signiﬁcant stakeholders
of the project. Therefore, an interview with the director and tourist chief for Odsherred
Geopark and Visit Odsherred, Hans-Jørgen Olsen was made. The questions and answers
can be found in appendix M. The interview had focus on his opinion on wind turbines
both from the Geopark’s point of view and the tourist board, the location of the turbine
sites and how the Geopark and tourist board could take advantage of the wind turbines
to increase their reputation and image. According to the website, the vision is to cre-
68
==PAGE:83==
ate sustainability in Odsherred. Hans-Jørgen explained this sustainability as creating
sustainable communities, sustainable growth and responsible consumption. He empha-
sized that a re-powering of the turbines could increase the responsible consumption of
the municipality and that they were committed to support the idea of the project only if
the turbines were placed outside the unique areas of the municipality. The unique areas
are the Odsherred arches and can be seen in ﬁgure 1.6, originating from the latest ice
age. These arches are protected by Unesco and this information also emphasizes that
in the case the turbine sites were placed inside these areas the project would have high
possibility to be scrapped. Hans-Jørgen had an positive attitude towards the selected
turbine sites. He mentions Sidinge Fjord to be an lawful area to site the turbines due to
the better landscape features compared to other areas in Odsherred. According to the
site located in Fårevejle he wanted to know the exact location of the turbine site since
some of the areas in Fårevejle are parts of the Odsherred arches and very valuable for
the Dragsholm castle. However, the located site in Fårevejle, after a brief discussion was
clearly considered a part of lammefjorden and seen as not having an impact on the castle
and landscape according to Hans-Jørgen. In order to secure if the turbines were placed
outside the arches, a resource grid on the WAsP vector map was applied. The vector
map can be seen in ﬁgure 9.1. The grid shows the elevation level of the area. From the
ﬁgure it can be conﬁrmed that the turbine sites are placed outside the arches since the
elevation level of the sites is very low.
69
==PAGE:84==
Figure 9.1: The Odsherred arches shown in WAsP vector map. With the help of the resource grid function, the elevation
of the map can be seen. The red and orange areas are the Odsherred arches.
In accordance with tourism, Hans-Jørgen was less conﬁdent. He believes that wind energy
can have an important role of giving the municipality a sustainable image but not as an
attraction for tourists. He compares it with the solar heating project which was very
popular in the beginning of the project among the inhabitants of Odsherred. He also
stated, that if the turbines were placed correct, a less unfortunate eﬀect on tourism
would be seen. Activities such as turbine excursion and climbing were something the
tourist board had done earlier when the ﬁrst turbines in lammefjorden were conﬁgured.
He believes it can have a good eﬀect in the initial phase of the project but not necessarily
in a longer period of time.
9.4
Sommerland Sjælland
Sommerland Sjælland is an amusement park located close to Nørre Asminderup for fami-
lies with children. The park carries an important role to Visit Odsherred since it attracts
many tourists during the summer season. It was obvious during the interview with the
Tourist Chief to ask him, what he thought about the idea to place a symbolic turbine
close to the amusement park. His thoughts were positive, since it backs up the goal of
having a responsible consumption in the municipality, but also giving them a sustainable
image. The park is open from mid-May to mid-September. Contact with the park owner,
70
==PAGE:85==
Kåre Dyvekær has been made (see appendix M). His opinion towards the idea is positive.
He thinks it can be a good way to increase the reputation of his park. According to
the owner, the park has an annual energy consumption of 0.3-0.4 GWh. Most of the
consumption is during the season where the park has visitors. This consumption can be
covered easily by the ﬁve turbines placed in Sidinge and Fårevejle but the park will not
have the green energy symbolism, the owner prefers to have during the e-mail interview.
He also expresses his excitement to the idea and that it can be a way to "brag" to the
visitors and other amusement parks in Denmark about sustainability. He wants the tur-
bine to be placed close thus it can be visible from the entrance. He wants to impress
his visitors by explanatory text and arrow pointing toward the turbine. This idea which
Kåre during the interview (appendix M) mentions, supports the idea achieved together
with the municipality. The tourist chief Hans-Jørgen also expressed his support during
the interview (appendix M).
Figure 9.2: Two wind turbine sites can be seen in the ﬁgure close to the amusement park.
To realize the idea, it requires to locate a new turbine site. Due to the requirements
explained in chapter 4 it is not possible to locate the site just beside the park. Conse-
quently, two turbine sites have been found which is shown in ﬁgure 9.2. The ﬁrst site
is located in Svinninge, which was a part of the EIA and explained in table 4.2. The
area is close to the Trundholm bog where the solvogn was found. Also, a cenotaph of
the solvogn (sun chariot) is located. On that account, this area is very sensitive to a
turbine site and the turbine has to be large in order to be visible from the park entrance
which is located 2 km away. The second turbine site is closer to the entrance. Here,
71
==PAGE:86==

requirement for residential. In the present WT-market it is diﬃcult to ﬁnd small-scale
onshore turbines due to the less demand. Although, two "small" WT-models by Enercon
were found which is shown in table 9.2.

==PAGE:87==
9.5
Ownership Models
The development of wind power has been going through a paradigm shift throughout the
years. In the beginning of the Danish wind history, the wind turbines were owned and
erected by local groups. The ﬁrst series of the wind turbines in the 1970s had a capacity of
22-50 kW, this has increased tremendously throughout the years. The latest onshore wind
turbine model has a capacity of 4 MW (2018). The increased size of the wind turbines has
increased the wind turbine price as well. These small scale wind turbines did not require
a major investment compared to wind turbines today. Expensive wind turbines make it
harder for the locals to pay for a local turbine and thereby get a share in the project.
Throughout the years the number of local owned wind turbines has decreased. This has
resulted in an increased resistance from the locals where the transition from wind turbine
cooperatives and small private owner to the domination of professionalized, commercial
project developers has played a major role regarding the locals opinion against wind
projects[25].

In table 9.4 an overview over the various ownership models are presented. The distribution
of ownership models are mainly based on the size of the project. For the co-operatives
and the enterprise groups the size of the wind project is typically below 10 MW while
the large scale wind project is owned by medium private companies as well as the large
utilities and private corporations[25]. With the decreed issued by the Danish government
in 2011 stating that 20% of the wind farms should be oﬀered to the nearby locals, this
could help avoid conﬂicts that could arise when projects are proposed. Since the people
living near the proposed projects would most likely be more inclined of the acceptance of
the project[4]. This could especially be relevant for the involved cottage and landowners
close to the turbine sites. It is suﬃcient to inform the locals who lives near the area
73
==PAGE:88==
about the project in order to obtain their trust. This can be done by the municipality
by arranging conferences about the project, the SEP and the mutual beneﬁts.
9.6
Sub-conclusion
Communication with the signiﬁcant stakeholders regarding the project acceptance has
been made. The municipality, Odsherred Geopark and the tourist board Visit Odsherred
were considered to be the most signiﬁcant. The municipality wants the project to be
realized but fears the attitudes toward the project, especially the stakeholders within
tourism. Therefore, an interview with the director and tourist chief Hans-Jørgen Olsen
was made in order to have his opinions toward the project. The attitude of the director
was in overall positive as long as the unique areas of the municipality were not harmed
which he described as the Odsherred arches (appendix M). The director was satisﬁed
with the locations of the sites even though the turbine site located in Fårevejle was fairly
close to the castle and the Odsherred arches. He was pleased with the idea of the sym-
bolic turbine which was planned to be located close to the amusement park Sommerland
Sjælland. He believed it would increase the image of the amusement park as well as the
tourist board.
Kåre Dyvekær, the owner of the amusement park was satisﬁed with the idea of the sym-
bolic turbine and shared his willingness to support the idea during the email interview
(appendix M). Although the extra turbine being unnecessary for the municipality, the cli-
mate coordinator, Simone Veber, believed it could increase the reputation of wind energy
and thereby be a good way to promote wind energy in Odsherred. It was not recom-
mended to place the turbine in the area of Svinninge since the area very sensitive due
to the found of the solvogn (sun chariot). The best solution is to place a small turbine
closer to the entrance so that the visitors can be able to see it.
74
==PAGE:89==
10. Solar Wind Combination
In this chapter an alternative solution is investigated based on a combination of solar and
wind power. This will be performed in order to comply with the CO2 requirements. In
chapter 10 it was found that ﬁve WT were to be installed where three WT were placed
in Sidinge Fjord and the remaining two in Fårevejle. Since Sidinge Fjord had a higher
energy output and less environmental impact compared to Fårevjle. The decision was
made to replace the two WT in Fårevejle with solar power, though at a site that is more
potential for siting of solar power. The proposed project is a utility scale solar farm
and will be designed to cover the production of 22.51 GWh for Fårevejle see table 6.1.
Furthermore, it is decided to site the solar farm at Hagesholm since it is expected that
the environmental impact would be small due to the nearby wind turbines this is also
the area which the municipality has selected for future wind turbine planning [34], the
area can be seen in appendix O ﬁgure O.1. Additionally the location is well suited for
the solar farm due to a ﬂat terrain. The location of the site is illustrated in appendix L
ﬁgure L.1. The analysis will be carried out with the PVsyst software tool [44].
Firstly the assumptions made to simulate the solar farm will be treated followed by a
study of the three technologies consisting monocrystalline, polycrystalline, thin ﬁlm for
varying tilt angles and azimuth angle as well as diﬀerent ventilation properties. Then
ﬁxed active area analysis for the three technologies will be presented followed with the
monthly energy production. Lastly an economic analysis will be presented shortly, that
concludes the chapter.
10.1
Assumptions
To calculate the energy production for the solar farm in PVsyst assumptions have to be
performed. The ﬁrst assumption made is that the Meteonorm 7.2 station in Holbæk is
representative for the weather conditions in Hagesholm see appendix L for setup. Then
the horizon shading is set to zero assuming that no shading is present on the active area
for the solar panels. During the calculations the annual yield is held ﬁxed at 22.51 GWh
unless otherwise is speciﬁed. Furthermore, it should be mentioned that the calculations
are done for a preliminary design and are grid connected.
75
==PAGE:90==
10.2
Sensitivity analysis
10.2.1
Tilt angle analysis
In ﬁgure 10.1 a diagram over the three technologies can be seen as a function of the tilt
angle. It is noticed how the thin ﬁlm requires a much larger active area of solar panels
in order to cover the energy demand while monocrystalline and polycrystalline have a
smaller area, though the monocrystalline yields the best results. Furthermore it is noticed
how the zero tilt angle leads to the largest active area whereas a more eﬃcient tilt angle
is considered to be a 45 °.
Figure 10.1: Area as function of tilt angle for the three technologies
To elaborate further on the most optimal tilt angle a separate study for monocrystalline
has been carried out since it yields the smallest required area. This can be seen in ﬁgure
10.2.
76
==PAGE:91==
Figure 10.2: Area for monocrystalline as a function of tilt angle
It is observed how the diﬀerence in the active area is very small in the interval of 30-55°
which shows that the solar farm will be eﬃcient at these tilt angles. The required active
area is almost equal for the tilt angles of 40° and 45°, though the precise active area for
the 40°tilt angle yields 123510 m2 while the 45° tilt angle leads to a lower active area of
123409 m2. The most optimal angle is observed at a tilt angle of 45° since the active area
increase with an increasing tilt angle and therefore used for the subsequent calculations.
10.2.2
Azimuth angle analysis
In this section it is desired to study the orientation of the solar panels along with the three
technologies. The results which are illustrated in ﬁgure 10.3 show that the most eﬀective
azimuth angle is 0°, which is deﬁned as South in PVsyst as the sun rises in East and sets
in West. The monocrystalline technology yields the lowest active area close followed by
the polycrystalline technology.

10.2.5
Monthly energy distribution
The investigation of the monthly energy production is presented in this section. In ﬁgure
10.5 the results are shown. As expected the summer period from May to July yields the
highest energy production while the production in January and December is very low.
The results have great importance due to the solar/wind combination since the winter
brings a more windy weather and thereby a higher energy production. This leads to a
more stable energy production where the energy supply could supply the municipality
throughout the whole year. The detailed calculations and system setup for the proposed
PV solar farm can be seen in appendix L.

10.3
Economics
Since the default values in PVsyst is outdated and results in high investment prices, the
economy will be treated on updated prices and presented in this section. The values
used to compute the solar PV farm economy will be based on the IRENA renewable
power generations costs [24]. The calculation will be performed for the monocrystalline
technology, with a zero azimuth angle, 45° tilt angle and a free standing ventilation
property as it led to the most eﬃcient solar farm design, furthermore the economy will
be calculated during a 20 year lifetime.
The installation cost includes the soft cost,
installation cost and the hardware cost, where the detailed description of the costs can
be seen in [24]. Since the O&M cost was only available for the United States it is assumed
that Denmark has the same price [24]. The prices are for utility-scale solar PV. Lastly, the
electricity price is assumed to be 291 DKK/MWh, equal to the wind energy economics.

while the electricity sales would bring 131 mil. DKK. Since the payback time will never
be reached for the proposed project leading to a negative net income of approx. 42 mil.
DKK, the project would not be feasible. However it should be mentioned that each large
81
==PAGE:96==
plant is a negotiation and therefore the prices can vary a lot. As the PV don’t have
a super economy in large sizes when selling to the grid except for the prices gained by
IRENA [24] many challenges have been encountered during the economic calculations.
Normally the best economy is based on self consumption when you can have a saving
value of 2 DKK/kWh. If you have to sell all PV production to the grid without subsidies
added the saving value can be less than half of the 2 DKK/kWh saving value.

==PAGE:97==
11. Summary and Conclusion
To conclude, the main ﬁndings will be presented in a brief summary of this thesis. Based
on these ﬁndings, suggestions for further work are given.
11.1
Summary
As a part of the Strategic Energy Plan of the municipality, the thesis has been undertaken
with the aim of re-powering the existing wind turbines located in Odsherred. The thesis
had focus on the recent goal of reducing the amount of CO2 emissions by 20% by 2020
compared to 2008. The wind resource was assessed within an available area, which was
determined from the ﬁndings of an EIA investigation focused on: observed cottages, visual
impact, noise and ﬂicker requirements and a brief landscape analysis of the municipality.
AEP estimations of the ﬁve wind turbine sites located in Sidinge Fjord and Fårevejle were
performed with the software WAsP. The economic feasibility of the proposed project was
carried out. The key ﬁnancial indicators of the project were reported and a sensitivity
analysis of the results was carried out. The grid connection was presented where points of
connection as well as the needed voltage level were studied. The important stakeholders of
the project were presented. The attitudes of the stakeholders were described by interviews
and solutions to ease the project acceptance were presented. Lastly, an alternative hybrid
solution, combining solar and wind, was investigated.
11.2
Conclusion
The size of the installed capacity is determined to be 20 MW. This means, the new
wind turbines have to yield an annual energy production of 53 GWh in order to comply
with the required reduction of CO2 emissions. The results of the EIA study revealed that
wind turbine siting can be an achievement even inside the most unique landscapes. The
results pointed at Sidinge Fjord and Fårevejle as the ideal areas to site the new wind
turbines. The reduction can be achieved by siting ﬁve wind turbines in total, respectively
three in Sidinge Fjord and two in Fårevejle. It can be concluded that it will best beneﬁt
the municipality to use these two areas due to their signiﬁcant advantages they present in
terms of noise, shadow ﬂicker requirements, landscape, and the number of cottages
nearby. Also, the visualizations of the crucial points of the areas show the visual impact
to be very low on the landscape, respectively in Sidinge Fjord and Fårevejle. It is further
83
==PAGE:98==
recommended to decommission the existing 11 wind turbines due to their exceedance of
lifespan, but also to the fact that, they have a small energy production of 5.7 GWh
(2018). Also, the decommissioning is believed to give the new wind turbines an increased
acceptance from the locals and stakeholders within the municipality, since the visual im-
pact on the landscape is cleared from the existent turbines.
The chosen WAsP model with the SRTM map and Risø mast was used to estimate the
AEP of the wind turbine sites in Sidinge Fjord and Fårevejle.
The turbine models,
Siemens SWT - 4.0 - 120 and Vestas V117 - 4.2, yielded the highest AEP estima-
tions and are recommended to be selected. The ﬁve wind turbines can fulﬁll the required
reduction of CO2 emissions if these WT models are used. It can be concluded that, the
obtained AEP estimations of WT sites are reliable results due to the applied technical
losses as well as the uncertainty factors and the way the WAsP models were built with
diﬀerent maps and generalized wind climates. The long-term energy correction on the
AEP results made the results even more realistic. The WAsP model, including the Risø
mast and SRTM vector map yielded the closest AEP estimation of the existing turbine
sites in Sidinge, therefore, this model was used during all simulations. It is believed that
the results could be more correct if a closer wind mast was accessible, since the Risø mast
was located far away.
The wind turbine sites found in the EIA study can be validated to be a correct deter-
mination, since the director of Geopark Odsherred had a positive attitude towards the
project overall and most important the location of the turbine sites. The attitude of
the director made the municipality more conﬁdent regarding the project, since they had
concerns about the wind turbines impact on the landscape to start with. The attitude
of the director also indicates the success of the project. The aim was to create a link be-
tween the tourism and the municipality, and it is believed that the project proved that by
including the symbolic wind turbine concept into a realization by contacting the director
of Sommerland Sjælland. Therefore, it is concluded that wind turbines and tourism can
go hand in hand if a beneﬁcial solution for the stakeholder is found.
A realistic grid connection to the local grid of the municipality were located for the tur-
bine sites in Sidinge Fjord and Fårevejle respectively. The turbine site in Sidinge Fjord
can be connected to the grid station located north to Vig, which is about 6.6 km away
from the turbines. The turbine site in Fårevejle can be coupled to the grid located in
Ris, approximately 3.8 km away from the turbines. Both sites were connected with a
voltage level of 50/10 kV. The local grid company, Cerius, suggested to have an export
level of 10 kV due to the size of the project being small. This would be the cheapest solu-
84
==PAGE:99==
tion for the developer but would yield a higher transmission loss of the energy production.
From the results obtained in the project economy, it can be concluded that the project
is proﬁtable with the assumed electricity price of 291 DKK/MWh. The Internal Rate of
Return, yielded 8.8 % which was above the assumed Discount Rate. From the sensitivity
analysis it can be concluded that, a decreasing electricity price of 231 DKK/MWh the
Internal Rate of Return would be 6.3 % which is quite close to the assumed discount
rate. This is considered to be an critical electricity price, since an further decreasing
price would result in a non-proﬁtable project. An alternative hybrid solution of solar
and wind power was investigated. The monocrystalline technology is concluded to be
the ideal choice since it requires a smaller active area to site. The sensitivity analysis of
monocrystalline shows a optimal design at a tilt angle of 45◦and an azimuth angle of 0◦.
Lastly, the solar economics show a nominal power of 20 MWp is required to cover the
energy demand. This is equal to the same amount of capacity needed for the whole wind
project which could be due to the fact that Denmark not being suited as a solar country
unlike warmer countries. The investment for the solar project is larger than the entire
wind project economy which makes the solar wind combination less favourable compared
to the proposed wind project.
11.3
Future Work
For future work in regards to the stakeholders, an further elaboration on the stakeholder
analysis would be interesting. A strategy could be developed in order to achieve the public
acceptance of the locals and thus cottage owners. This could be done by including the
described ownership models in chapter 9 in the analysis and by asking the locals opinion
on wind turbines if the recommended ownership models and shares were used. If their
opinions remained unchanged a new ownership model could be developed and suggested.
Furthermore, it would be interesting to make a model to forecast the electricity price,
since the future electricity price is very diﬃcult to predict. Although the uncertainties
and technical losses where chosen in the recommended interval given from the course
notes [7] and based on the wind turbine capacity, a more thorough site speciﬁc analysis
of the estimation of uncertainties and technical losses would be interesting to study in
order to improve the AEP output of the wind turbines. Lastly in regards of the AEP
estimation it would be desired to make measurements at the chosen sites in order to
get a more realistic AEP output as well as a thorough analysis of selecting the proper
IEC class. The measurements would include, wind speed, turbulence, wind shear, wind
direction and ﬂow inclination.
85

Appendices
v
==PAGE:105==
A. WAsP and WAT results
In this chapter, the six model results achieved with WAsP and WAT will be illustrated.
Some of them will include reports and some only results achieved from the WAT tool due
to the similarity of the reports. I addition, in some models, the work space hierarchy will
be shown, since they can change from model to model. Lastly, the calculations of the
long-term energy correction can be found.
A.1
OWC Risø Mast, SRTM Map Results
A.1.1
WAsP project report
The uploaded PDF-ﬁle down below is the wind farm report of the existing V47-turbines
located in Sidinge. The report is only for the combination of the Observed Wind Climate
imported from the mast located in Risø and the corresponding SRTM map created with
the vector map tool, since it was the model we chose to work with. The other wind
farm reports of the models are very similar, since the site is the same. The only details
which was changed are the generalized wind climate and the vector map. Also, a screen
shot of the WAsP work space is uploaded thus the hierarchy can be seen. The work
space hierarchy is very similar in other models and is therefore not included for the other
models. Lastly, the turbine site report is uploaded in order to show the gross annual
energy production of the turbine sites.

A.10
IEC-Standard with WAT
By importing the generalized wind climate (GWC) and 50 year extreme winds into the
Wind Assessment Tool (WAT), eﬀective turbulence plots can be estimated. This is done
to ensure the chosen wind turbine generator can withstand the wind climate at the site,
according to the IEC 61400-1 (ed.3) standard, which is a IEC-standard higher than the
turbines in Hagesholm have. According to WAT, the turbine sites located in Sidinge Fjord
do not pass the eﬀective turbulence intensity even in a very ﬂat terrain. It is reported to
be a typical WAT issue and might be due to the new software update. The issue can be
seen in ﬁgure A.13.
Figure A.13: Eﬀective turbulence intensity as function of wind speed. The selected IEC-standard do not exceed the eﬀective
turbulence intensity
In ﬁgure A.15, it is seen that the actual PDF is below the design PDF in the IEC range.
The WAT tool consider this to be OK.
Figure A.14: Wind-speed probability density distribution

DECIBEL - Hoved resultat
Støjberegningsmetode:
 Dansk 2011 og 2015
Beregning er baseret på "Bekendtgørelse nr. 1736 af 21/12/2015" fra Miljøministeriet.
Støjbelastningen fra vindmøller må ikke overstige følgende grænseværdier: (Vindhastigheder i
10 m højde)
1) I det mest støjbelastede punkt ved udendørs opholdsarealer højst 15 m fra al anden
beboelse end vindmølleejerens private beboelse i det åbne land:
   a) 44 dB(A) ved en vindhastighed på 8 m/s.
   b) 42 dB(A) ved en vindhastighed på 6 m/s.
2) I det mest støjbelastede punkt ved udendørs opholdsarealer i områder, der anvendes til
eller i lokalplan eller byplanvedtægt er udlagt til bolig-, institutions-, sommerhus- eller
kolonihaveformål eller som rekreative områder:
   a) 39 dB(A) ved en vindhastighed på 8 m/s.
   b) 37 dB(A) ved en vindhastighed på 6 m/s.
Lavfrekvent støj fra vindmøller må ikke overstige 20 dB indendørs ved vindhastigheder 6 og 8
m/s.
Støjgrænserne gælder ikke for ejendom der bebos af vindmølle ejer(e).
Alle koordinater er i
UTM (north)-WGS84 Zone: 32
Skala 1:75.000

DECIBEL - Detaljerede resultater
Støjberegningsmetode: Dansk 2011 og 2015
Forudsætninger
Beregnet L(DW) = LWA,ref + K + Dc - (Adiv + Aatm + Agr + Abar + Amisc) - Cmet
(når der regnes med terrændæmpning er Dc = Domega)
LWA,ref:
Lydtryk ved vindmølle
K:
Rentone
Dc:
Retningskorrektion
Adiv:
dæmpningen pga. geometri
Aatm:
dæmpningen pga. luftabsorbtion
Agr:
dæmpningen pga. terrænforhld
Abar:
dæmpningen pga. lægivere
Amisc:
dæmpningen af forskellige andre grunde
Cmet:
Meteorologisk korrektion
Beregningsresultater

DECIBEL - Hoved resultat
Støjberegningsmetode:
 Dansk 2011 og 2015
Beregning er baseret på "Bekendtgørelse nr. 1736 af 21/12/2015" fra Miljøministeriet.
Støjbelastningen fra vindmøller må ikke overstige følgende grænseværdier: (Vindhastigheder i
10 m højde)
1) I det mest støjbelastede punkt ved udendørs opholdsarealer højst 15 m fra al anden
beboelse end vindmølleejerens private beboelse i det åbne land:
   a) 44 dB(A) ved en vindhastighed på 8 m/s.
   b) 42 dB(A) ved en vindhastighed på 6 m/s.
2) I det mest støjbelastede punkt ved udendørs opholdsarealer i områder, der anvendes til
eller i lokalplan eller byplanvedtægt er udlagt til bolig-, institutions-, sommerhus- eller
kolonihaveformål eller som rekreative områder:
   a) 39 dB(A) ved en vindhastighed på 8 m/s.
   b) 37 dB(A) ved en vindhastighed på 6 m/s.
Lavfrekvent støj fra vindmøller må ikke overstige 20 dB indendørs ved vindhastigheder 6 og 8
m/s.
Støjgrænserne gælder ikke for ejendom der bebos af vindmølle ejer(e).
Alle koordinater er i
UTM (north)-WGS84 Zone: 32
Skala 1:75.000

DECIBEL - Hoved resultat
Støjberegningsmetode:
 Dansk 2011 og 2015
Beregning er baseret på "Bekendtgørelse nr. 1736 af 21/12/2015" fra Miljøministeriet.
Støjbelastningen fra vindmøller må ikke overstige følgende grænseværdier: (Vindhastigheder i
10 m højde)
1) I det mest støjbelastede punkt ved udendørs opholdsarealer højst 15 m fra al anden
beboelse end vindmølleejerens private beboelse i det åbne land:
   a) 44 dB(A) ved en vindhastighed på 8 m/s.
   b) 42 dB(A) ved en vindhastighed på 6 m/s.
2) I det mest støjbelastede punkt ved udendørs opholdsarealer i områder, der anvendes til
eller i lokalplan eller byplanvedtægt er udlagt til bolig-, institutions-, sommerhus- eller
kolonihaveformål eller som rekreative områder:
   a) 39 dB(A) ved en vindhastighed på 8 m/s.
   b) 37 dB(A) ved en vindhastighed på 6 m/s.
Lavfrekvent støj fra vindmøller må ikke overstige 20 dB indendørs ved vindhastigheder 6 og 8
m/s.
Støjgrænserne gælder ikke for ejendom der bebos af vindmølle ejer(e).
Alle koordinater er i
UTM (north)-WGS84 Zone: 32
Skala 1:75.000

DECIBEL - Hoved resultat
Støjberegningsmetode:
 Dansk 2011 og 2015
Beregning er baseret på "Bekendtgørelse nr. 1736 af 21/12/2015" fra Miljøministeriet.
Støjbelastningen fra vindmøller må ikke overstige følgende grænseværdier: (Vindhastigheder i
10 m højde)
1) I det mest støjbelastede punkt ved udendørs opholdsarealer højst 15 m fra al anden
beboelse end vindmølleejerens private beboelse i det åbne land:
   a) 44 dB(A) ved en vindhastighed på 8 m/s.
   b) 42 dB(A) ved en vindhastighed på 6 m/s.
2) I det mest støjbelastede punkt ved udendørs opholdsarealer i områder, der anvendes til
eller i lokalplan eller byplanvedtægt er udlagt til bolig-, institutions-, sommerhus- eller
kolonihaveformål eller som rekreative områder:
   a) 39 dB(A) ved en vindhastighed på 8 m/s.
   b) 37 dB(A) ved en vindhastighed på 6 m/s.
Lavfrekvent støj fra vindmøller må ikke overstige 20 dB indendørs ved vindhastigheder 6 og 8
m/s.
Støjgrænserne gælder ikke for ejendom der bebos af vindmølle ejer(e).
Alle koordinater er i
UTM (north)-WGS84 Zone: 32
Skala 1:125.000

F. Maps
F.1
Google Earth Maps
Figure F.1 shows the potential areas found in the EIA analyses for the wind turbines
with a total height of 100 m. This map is fairly similar to the one in the report. Larger
areas to site is likely to be found due to the decreased wind turbine size. This map was
not used since we chose to work with 150 m wind turbine size.
Figure F.1: Potential wind turbine location for 100 m wind turbines
c
==PAGE:200==
F.2
How a Vector Map Is Created
Figure F.2: How to create a vector map from the dataset of the global wind atlas. The data has a 3 arc-second resolution
and is mainly based on data collected by the Shuttle Radar Topography Mission (SRTM).
When importing the data set from the Global Wind Atlas in the map editor tool, a pro-
jection type must be chosen. Since Denmark is located north of equator the northern
hemisphere projection is selected. The coordinates of the centre of Odsherred are imple-
mented from Google Earth to the map editor with a map extension of 50000mx50000m.

I. Other Stakeholders Explained
I.0.1
Landowners
In the western and eastern side of the site households is observed how most of the house-
hold consists of farmers as illustrated in ﬁgure 4.2. Since the farmers has a lot of land it is
expected that that some of the area for the site is owned by the neighbouring households.
Therefore the landowners has to be considered. It is crucial for the advancement of the
project to deal with the issue correctly. Including the landowners early in the process
might give a positive attitude towards the project. This also gives the landowners a sense
of importance by giving them a voice. The lost farmland has to be compensated and
also oﬀering shares is a possibility. Convincing the landowner about the project being a
good investment is essential for the planning process. Another approach to make sure the
project progresses smoothly is to include the agriculture association, since the association
could represent a large proportion of the landowners.
I.0.2
Associations
The purpose of the Danish Nature protected association in Odsherred[39] is to
work towards preserving the nature and the protected areas in the municipality. The
studies made in section 4.3.1 showed that although the protection lines were outside the
potential site a couple of areas with trees were present in the site area therefore it can be
expected that the association would have an opposing attitude toward the wind turbine
project. To reduce the resistance from the association the communication with the asso-
ciation must be maintained on regular basis.
Another stakeholder that have to be handled with care is the tourism association[51].
Although the population of the area is low there are still cottages to consider along with
the eﬀect of the landscape and visual impact that the tourist will be met by. In order to
get the acceptance of the association various actions can be used, where some of them
involves arranging events and designing the layout of the wind farm as mentioned in 4.3.1.
This could turn the wind farm to a more positive attraction. Therefore the communica-
tion with the association and the level of communication must be on a reasonable level
so the association feel involved in the early stages of the project.
Then there is the churches to consider from ﬁgure 4.2 the distances from the churches
cviii
==PAGE:208==
to the potential site is illustrated. It is noted that the church in Vig and Egebjerg has
a distance of 3.9 and 2.4 km respectively.
With a distance closer than 28 times the
total height of the turbines, the churches has the right to veto the project. Therefore
the churches must be included in the process in order to get the churches approval. An
advantage in the planning of the project is that the church of Egebjerg is a green church
and is likely to be more open towards the project.
In Odsherred there is the association sustainability initiative now[38] which could
have a great advantage in the project. The union is a association of diﬀerent parties that
strives to get a more environmentally friendly and sustainable development in the future.
By focusing on CO2 emissions and renewable energy the union hopes to make a diﬀerence.
This could be a great advantage for the developer, since the the union advocates for a
greener society. Therefore it would be an advantage if possible to include the union in
order to change the local and other associations toward a more positive attitude about
the project.
Lastly there is the housing cooperative Fri & Fro that are placed in Egebjerg which are
striving to built and live economical. The goal of the association is to built sustainable
houses and could therefore have an signiﬁcance during the planning phase. The vision
of sustainability might angle to emphasize on in order to get the acceptance of the as-
sociation. However it is expected that Fri Fro would have their concerns regarding the
valuation of the households.
I.0.3
Residential owners
Residential and cottage owners must also be taken into account, since the new turbines
in the nearby area could impact the property value. A way of getting the acceptance of
the owners could be to compensate for the lost value of the properties.

==PAGE:229==
M. Interviews with stakeholders
M.1
The Odsherred Geopark and Tourist board
In this section, the interview with the director and touristchef of Odsherred Geopark and
Visit Odsherred, Hans-Jørgen Olsen can be found.
cxxx
==PAGE:230==
Interview med Geopark og turistchef for Odsherred.  
 
Hans-Jørgen Olsen 
 
 
- 
Hvad er din overordnede holdning til vindmøller som turistchef for Odsherred og 
direktør for Geo Parken? 
- 
Som udgangspunkt er vores holdning at give plads til vedvarende energi. Så er der altid 
en række problemer når man bor i Danmarks største sommerhus kommune, hvor der 
25.000 sommerhuse. Vi er klar over at det er et ømsigtigt punkt at have store vind 
møller ud mod kysten.  
- 
Det skal dog siges, at vindmøllerne skal placeres på land, da det er et kommunalt 
projekt. Og i den anledning synes vi, at det er relevant at vide, hvad din holdning, 
som både turist og direktør for VisitOdsherred og Geo Park er.  
- 
Altså, der ligger jo i forvejen nogle vindmøller på lammefjorden. Så det man kan sige er, 
at det sted er et relativt godt sted at ligge dem. Hvis man nu tager Geo Park brillerne 
på, så er de her Odsherred buer, altså vejr højbuerne osv. et meget karakteristisk træk i 
landskabet, hvorfor vi specielt ikke vil være begejstret for at man i disse unikke steder 
satte vindmøller op.  
- 
Vi har enten tænkt os at placere vindmøllerne i Fårevejle, hvilket er tæt på 
Dragsholmslot og i Sidinge Fjord. Hvad er din umiddelbare mening om de to 
placeringer?  
- 
Sidinge Fjord har bedre landskabelige træk end lammefjorden og vil være en bedre 
mulighed end lammefjorden. Når det kommer til Fårevejle, er det vigtigt at vide hvor i 
Fårevejle?  
- 
Det sted vi har tænkt kan beskrives som et kæmpe landsbrugs areal tæt på Fårevejle 
Stationsby.  
- 
Det tilhører jo lammefjorden og det er ikke i nærheden af Dragsholmslot til at have en 
betydning. Men jeg synes umiddelbart, at Sidinge fjord virker som en mere oplagt 
placering grundet landskabets karakteristiske træk i forhold til lammefjorden. Men 
umiddelbart synes jeg, at lammefjorden og det sted du beskriver også en oplagt 
placering.  
- 
Vores andet spørgsmål er om, hvorvidt landmøller kan fremme jeres image som et 
Geo Park da ifølge jeres webside går ind for bæredygtighed.  
- 
Der er ikke nogen tvivl om, at de her FN verdensmål er noget som Geo Parken er 
forpligtet til at arbejde med. Og i år har vi udvalgt tre bæredygtighedsmål som vi har 
fokus på og det er: bæredygtige lokalsamfund, bæredygtigvækst og ansvarligt forbrug. 
Her kan man sige, at vindmøller spiller positivt ind med de her verdensmål. Som 
udgangspunkt set med Geo Park øjne vil øget produktion af vedvarende energi støtte 
op omkring disse Geoparks mål bl.a. ansvarligt forbrug.  
- 
Hvad så med indenfor turismen? Vil det have et godt image for turismen i 
kommunen?  
- 
Altså, nej der er jeg nok mere tvivlende. Hvis de placeres rigtigt, ville det ikke have en 
uheldig virkning. Det kan ligge noget til, det at være en bæredygtig destination, det er 
==PAGE:231==
klart. Vi har set det lidt med solvarme projektet placeret lidt udefra Nykøbing Sjælland. 
Det har jo haft en ganske positiv effekt og understøttet det image du snakker om. Men 
man kan ikke se på det som en turist tilstrømning pga. det. Men man kan jo sige, at det 
vil understøtte det image i at have et ansvarligt forbrug.  
- 
Kan det ikke realiseres i form af aktiviteter som fx vindmølle udflugt og forklaring om 
moderne vindmøller?  
- 
De aktiviteter lavede vi jo også dengang, da den første vindmøllepark blev sat op i 
lammefjorden i de første par år. Også når det jo et vendingspunkt også kommer der 
noget nyt. Men jeg tror da godt det er en opstart, altså i anlægsfasen og i begyndelsen 
kan være en realitet. 
- 
Vi har haft en samtale med Kåre Dyvekær omkring en symbolsk mindre vindmølle der 
kunne placeres i nærheden af Sommerland Sjælland som vil forsyne 
forlystelsesparken og fremme dens image indenfor bæredygtighed. Hvad synes du 
umiddelbart om denne idé?  
- 
Jeg synes det lyder som en rigtig god idé. Det støtter op omkring vores mål i at have 
ansvarligt forbrug. Og mere har jeg ikke sige til det.  
- 
Tak for interviewet.  
- 
Selv tak og god pinse. 
- 
Jo tak og i lige måde.

Okay det lyder rigtig godt. Vi er i gang med at gøre hele projektet klar. Alle beregninger; hvor
møllerne skal placeres, valg af møller, AEP estimater og meget mere. Vi har tænkt os at skrive et
afsnit om turisme, hvor Sommerland Sjælland sammen med GeoParken vil blive inddraget og
hvordan vindmøller

brugt det så aktivt. Årsagen til at det samarbejde sluttede var, at det selskab ikke kunne fakturerer
bagud for det faktiske forbrug, og når der var aconto frem og tilbage mistede jeg overblikket. Så
udover grønt og miljørigtigt, skal det også være nemt at være kunde ifht. Overblik og afregning af ens
el.

Emne: Placering af Vindmølle
 
Hej Kåre, 
 
Jeg har vedhæftet et billede der viser, hvor vindmøllen kan sættes op. Pga. afstandkrave og
støjkrav er det ikke muligt at placere vindmøller tæt på et bebygget område. Cirka 2 km
(måske lidt mindre, alt efter møllens total højde) er det tætteste møllen kan placeres med
mindre, du har grunde, tæt på forlystelsesparken, hvor møllen kan opstilles. Møllen kommer
mindst til at have en total højde på 70m da mindre møller ikke ﬁndes på markedet. 
 
Hvad er din umiddelbare mening om dette. Ville det være ok for dig, hvis turbinen lå cirka 2
km fra forlystelsen indgang? 
 
Venlig hilsen, 
 
 
Timur & Mikael. 
DTU Vindenergi.
